<span id="freeTextContainer8245564621970923547"><strong>This is not a fairy tale. This is about <em>real</em> witches.</strong><br /><br />Grandmamma loves to tell about witches. Real witches are the most dangerous of all living creatures on earth. There's nothing they hate so much as children, and they work all kinds of terrifying spells to get rid of them. Her grandson listens closely to Grandmamma's stories - but nothing can prepare him for the day he co</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8245564621970923547"><strong>This is not a fairy tale. This is about <em>real</em> witches.</strong><br /><br />Grandmamma loves to tell about witches. Real witches are the most dangerous of all living creatures on earth. There's nothing they hate so much as children, and they work all kinds of terrifying spells to get rid of them. Her grandson listens closely to Grandmamma's stories - but nothing can prepare him for the day he comes face to face with The Grand High Witch herself!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1102833">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1102833" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/71852-jessica" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1178038599p2/71852.jpg" alt="Jessica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1102833?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 08, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/71852-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/71852-jessica?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1102833">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6260845152530398111">Warning: Extremely Long Review and Childhood Storytelling<br /><br />When I was ten or eleven, I was sitting in the playground at summer camp, minding my own business and reading this book, when one of the playground supervisers came and asked me what I was reading. When I showed it to him, his eyes got wide and he took the book from me. Then he went to the trash can and started ripping it up, page by page. And he washed his hands afterwards, "to get rid of the filth." It was a <em>library book</em>. He was just goi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6260845152530398111">Warning: Extremely Long Review and Childhood Storytelling<br /><br />When I was ten or eleven, I was sitting in the playground at summer camp, minding my own business and reading this book, when one of the playground supervisers came and asked me what I was reading. When I showed it to him, his eyes got wide and he took the book from me. Then he went to the trash can and started ripping it up, page by page. And he washed his hands afterwards, "to get rid of the filth." It was a <em>library book</em>. He was just going on and on about how young children shouldn't read about witchcraft because they might want to become witches, etc. etc. If you've read the book, you know that Dahl doesn't exactly idealize witches. Well, when my dad came to pick me up, he let this guy have it (yay Dad!) and I got a popsicle. So the story ends well, but I always remember this incident when I see this book. And because of that, this book is what I think of when I consider censorship and how detrimental it is to our society. I barely remember what happens in <em>The Witches</em>, but I love it simply because of what it represents to me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6260845152530398111">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/109490720?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 30, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1036930-michael" class="user" title="Michael">Michael</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=childrens-books" class="actionLinkLite">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=1980s" class="actionLinkLite">1980s</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer109490720">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11890067057682589086">I was a very sheltered child. <br /><br />Or was I a wuss? I was probably a wuss. <br /><br />For instance, when I was a little tot, Sammy Terry scared the shit out of me. I remember being frightened by commercials of the Nightmare on Elm Street movies, and the one time I inadvertently saw part of a Friday the 13th movie on TV? Fogettaboutit. Nightmares for weeks. <br /><br />But that all came later. <br /><br />But this book. Oh, this was traumatic shit. <br /><br />I was in preschool, probably 4 years old, when the teacher decided to read us The Witche</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11890067057682589086">I was a very sheltered child. <br /><br />Or was I a wuss? I was probably a wuss. <br /><br />For instance, when I was a little tot, Sammy Terry scared the shit out of me.  I remember being frightened by commercials of the Nightmare on Elm Street movies, and the one time I inadvertently saw part of a Friday the 13th movie on TV? Fogettaboutit. Nightmares for weeks. <br /><br />But that all came later. <br /><br />But this book. Oh, this was traumatic shit. <br /><br />I was in preschool, probably 4 years old, when the teacher decided to read us The Witches. Every day we'd sit on the carpet and listen to a little bit more, and . . . well, witches! Witches were frickin' scary at four, it didn't matter how cartoony they looked on the cover. I knew that real witches were scary looking and ugly. And *SPOILER ALERT* when that one kid got turned into a mouse, it scared me so bad I cried! I cried in front of the other kids, and they all thought I was a wuss! <br /><br />When I got home, I told my mom about crying in front of the class, and SHE WAS SOOOOO pissed. She called the teacher that night and expressed her displeasure with great verbosity and eloquence, probably traumatizing the teacher every bit as much as The Witches traumatized me. <br /><br />What happened the next day? We switched books. I can't remember the book that followed The Witches; it didn't scare me, whatever it was. Nobody found out what happened to the little kid who got turned into a mouse. For me, he will forever be a mouse. But at least we little chillens didn't have to hear about any more witches.<br /><br />A happy ending? More of an ambiguous one. Just a couple weeks later, my parents withdrew me from the school after I, in passing, told mom that the teacher gave her two favorite students ice cream bars during lunch, but never gave anyone else one. <br /><br />(I wasn't a tattle tale, I promise. I was just very talkative. And a wuss.)</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9721352">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15729122933616030098">I've noticed for years and years that critics love to say that Roald Dahl is "spinning in his grave" over some such filmic adaptation of his works. I'm a curious type person so I had to look up what the hell was in his grave, anyway. He was buried with pool cues, his typewriter and pencils (backup?). Guess he'd need to hustle his way past the pearly gates? I'm kidding! Don't dance on my grave. (Gosh, real critics are so <em>harsh</em>.) If he's spinning I guess there's plenty in there to make lots of rac</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15729122933616030098">I've noticed for years and years that critics love to say that Roald Dahl is "spinning in his grave" over some such filmic adaptation of his works. I'm a curious type person so I had to look up what the hell was in his grave, anyway. He was buried with pool cues, his typewriter and pencils (backup?). Guess he'd need to hustle his way past the pearly gates? I'm kidding! Don't dance on my grave. (Gosh, real critics are so <em>harsh</em>.) If he's spinning I guess there's plenty in there to make lots of racket.<br />The movie wasn't <em>that</em> bad. Okay, the American kid was a weanie and the special effects were cheesey. But Anjelica Huston was scary and oversexed. That was kinda awesome.<br />I was a Dahl fanatic as a kid. We read most of them as school assignments, but not <em>The Witches</em> for some reason. Maybe 'cause they want to do bad things to children. (Hold up, Trunchbull of <em>Matilda</em> did nasty things to kids! Ah, but she had administrative permission, which fooled yet more administrative permissors into permitting their administrative permissions for further kid terrorizing. Only the ones who read, mind, like Matilda. Reading <em>Matilda</em>.) Anyway, it was funny and gruesome and nasty and I loved it. It still holds up to adult nasty senses of humor.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380237807i/681480.jpg" /><br />Dance, dance, dance!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154399819">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8220467789771451035">The witches of England have a plan to do away with ALL English children. This little Norwegian orphan boy and his grandmamma come up with a plan to do away with all English <em>witches</em> instead. When they've accomplished that task, the little boy is noticeably altered in size and appearance. He doesn't mind, though. He sets off cheerfully with his grandmamma on a grand tour to rid the entire WORLD of those evil witchy creatures. <br /><br />I've always known there were real witches in the world, because Mrs. Nai</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8220467789771451035">The witches of England have a plan to do away with ALL English children. This little Norwegian orphan boy and his grandmamma come up with a plan to do away with all English <em>witches</em> instead. When they've accomplished that task, the little boy is noticeably altered in size and appearance. He doesn't mind, though. He sets off cheerfully with his grandmamma on a grand tour to rid the entire WORLD of those evil witchy creatures. <br /><br />I've always known there were real witches in the world, because Mrs. Nail, my first grade teacher, was the Queen Witch of the Universe. If only I'd had this book, I could have convinced everyone else I was right about her. <br />If you suspect that someone you know could be a witch, check for the following: <br /><br />1)They <em>always</em> wear gloves to hide the curvy cat claws they have instead of fingernails. <br /><br />2)Real witches are always bald as a boiled egg, but they hide it with first-class wigs. The wigs make their bare scalps itch, so watch for head-scratchers. <br /><br />3)Witches have bigger nose-holes than ordinary folks, the better to sniff out little children with. <br /><br />4)The pupils of a witch's eyes will keep changing color as you look into them. They'll switch from fire to ice and send a shiver up your spine.<br /><br />5)Witches never have toes. Their feet have square ends. <br /><br />6)Their spit is blue, like ink.<br /><br />Once you've established that you have a bona fide witch on your hands, it's time to slip some Formula 86 into her food and watch the transformation. Lucky for you, the secret recipe for Formula 86 is right here in this book, courtesy of your friend Roald Dahl. <br />Happy witch hunting!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_2549487">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2549487" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/162057-sarafem" class="left imgcol" title="sarafem"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1185759358p2/162057.jpg" alt="sarafem" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/2549487?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 08, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/162057-sarafem" class="user" title="sarafem">sarafem</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/162057-sarafem?shelf=royally-sucked" class="actionLinkLite">royally-sucked</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/162057-sarafem?shelf=juvenile-7-to-10" class="actionLinkLite">juvenile-7-to-10</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2549487">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9968818921724143247">I would love to know why I am the only person on the planet who did not like this book. I tried to find some bad reviews on GoodReads, but the only one and two star reviews said things like "Bad no like mousey! dlksk djglsk diewqls!" I'm assuming they were in a foreign language and not written by a kid who could not type, but I was too lazy to click on the profiles. Maybe I should learn the language and go live there, where we can all unite in our hatred of this book.<br /><br />It seems to me that 90% of t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9968818921724143247">I would love to know why I am the only person on the planet who did not like this book. I tried to find some bad reviews on GoodReads, but the only one and two star reviews said things like "Bad no like mousey! dlksk djglsk diewqls!" I'm assuming they were in a foreign language and not written by a kid who could not type, but I was too lazy to click on the profiles. Maybe I should learn the language and go live there, where we can all unite in our hatred of this book.<br /><br />It seems to me that 90% of the reviews said things like "Scared the crap out of me as a kid, but I like it now." Except...this is supposed to be for kids? So why give it five stars when children can't read it without being frightened?<br /><br />As an adult I see that this book is about the power of imagination and the triumph of good over evil. I get it. As a teacher and a mother, I think it's the author's perverse attempt to terrify little kids. It's really funny as a grown-up to think about how you hated certain teachers and thought of them as witches; this book brings childhood nostalgia back for this reason. As a kid, though, you end up terrified that you'll see a violet glow in your teacher's eyes if he or she gets short or loses patience with you. I do enough scaring of children just by getting my job done; I don't need a book around that's going to convince kids that I am about to eat them too.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9968818921724143247">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/5448792-brendon-schrodinger" class="user" title="Brendon Schrodinger">Brendon Schrodinger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5448792-brendon-schrodinger?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer168588231">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12774798220232993784">Witches are out there. You're lucky you're reading this now. It means that a witch never got you as a child or you escaped from their clutches.<br /><br />Witches are demons and have the following features: they wear wigs, they have squared-off feet with no toes and they smell faintly like old urinal. They have an insatiable need to kill, maim and turn children into animals. They can't stand children because to them they smell like dog poo. <br /><br />And they love meetings. And they love forming a club.<br /><br />I swear I have</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12774798220232993784">Witches are out there. You're lucky you're reading this now. It means that a witch never got you as a child or you escaped from their clutches.<br /><br />Witches are demons and have the following features: they wear wigs, they have squared-off feet with no toes and they smell faintly like old urinal. They have an insatiable need to kill, maim and turn children into animals. They can't stand children because to them they smell like dog poo. <br /><br />And they love meetings. And they love forming a club.<br /><br />I swear I have worked with one or two witches in the past.<br /><br />Everyone knows this story, especially since the movies came out in the 90s. The movie came out just that bit late for me, however I did watch it later and I feel that it clouds my enjoyment of the story. With 'The Witches' I'm a text purist. It's the same with 'Matilda', the movie was too late and nowhere as good as the text.<br /><br />So, the story is that the main character's parents are killed in a crash and he goes to live with his grandmother who is Norwegian and knows a bit about witches. They go on a holiday and they meet up with the annual english meeting of witches.<br /><br />OR<br /><br />An old woman who is hell bent on revenge from childhood trauma baits a group of witches with her grandson so she can kill them all!! Yippee Kay Yay Mother Witches.<br /><br />You be the judge.<br /><br /><br />P.S. That story about the girl in the painting is <em>still</em> one of the most haunting stories I have ever read.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1306066840">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10185045672755742032">Readers in the Roald Dahl <em>know</em> come to his books with an understanding that PG-13 level violence and mayhem are a part of his charms. This fast moving tale doesn't let fans down; all of the recognizable Dahlian tropes are on display and we are rooting for the child all the way to the end.<br /><br />I had the extra bonus of having this read to me by my daughter. She's at the stage now where she tries on different accents for each character; her English accent was adorable. So, five stars for the book, five</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10185045672755742032">Readers in the Roald Dahl <em>know</em> come to his books with an understanding that PG-13 level violence and mayhem are a part of his charms. This fast moving tale doesn't let fans down; all of the recognizable Dahlian tropes are on display and we are rooting for the child all the way to the end.<br /><br />I had the extra bonus of having this read to me by my daughter. She's at the stage now where she tries on different accents for each character; her English accent was adorable. So, five stars for the book, five stars for Bel the bookreader.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer192274685">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1660447523167349739"><img width="400" height="267" class="escapedImg" alt="Headlands Hotel" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380355254i/707583._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />For people who don't already know: the hotel used in the movie actually exists. It's <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.headlandhotel.co.uk/">The Headlands Hotel</a>, Newquay, England, and I've eaten there several times. <br /><br />The staff are friendly and well aware of the relevant history. If you ask, they'll show you the room where the witches had their big meeting and the spot where the baby carriage nearly gets pushed off the cliff. The food is good, and you get a fantastic view over the bay, where people surf in summer. Recommended!</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1053831139" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks" class="left imgcol" title="Stacey (prettybooks)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1429995380p2/3533262.jpg" alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1053831139?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 09, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks" class="user" title="Stacey (prettybooks)">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=childrens-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">classics-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1053831139">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14561269441045718003"><em>This is a short blogpost taken from <a rel="nofollow" href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/16/thoughts-on-roald-dahl-the-bfg-the-witches-fantastic-mr-fox/">Thoughts on Roald Dahl: The BFG, The Witches &amp; Fantastic Mr. Fox</a>.</em><br /><br /><em>The Witches</em> was chosen as part of this year's <a rel="nofollow" href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/10/18/my-halloween-reads/" title="My Halloween Reads">Halloween Reads</a> and it was a perfect children's book for October! It was everything I hoped it would be from the very first page. Again, it made me think how spot on the adaptations are – they capture the tone of each book perfectly. <em>The Witches</em> is morbidly funny, terrifying and brilliantly inventive, and it'll make any child wonder whether witche</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14561269441045718003"><em>This is a short blogpost taken from <a rel="nofollow" href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/16/thoughts-on-roald-dahl-the-bfg-the-witches-fantastic-mr-fox/">Thoughts on Roald Dahl: The BFG, The Witches &amp; Fantastic Mr. Fox</a>.</em><br /><br /><em>The Witches</em> was chosen as part of this year's <a rel="nofollow" href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/10/18/my-halloween-reads/" title="My Halloween Reads">Halloween Reads</a> and it was a perfect children's book for October! It was everything I hoped it would be from the very first page. Again, it made me think how spot on the adaptations are – they capture the tone of each book perfectly. <em>The Witches</em> is morbidly funny, terrifying and brilliantly inventive, and it'll make any child wonder whether witches <em>really</em> exist; they'll certainly know how to spot them after reading this book. If only Roald Dahl had written much longer stories. Can you imagine how fantastic these books would be if they were full-length novels? <em>The Witches</em> is perfectly creepy, but as with most Roald Dahl stories (I haven't read them all yet!), with an edge of dark humour. You don't see many characters like the boy's grandmother in children's literature now! She may be unconventional, but she adores her grandson and will do anything to help him save himself from the Witches' horrendous plans.<br /><br /><em>I am not, of course, telling you for one second that your teacher actually is a witch. All I am saying is that she might be one. It is most unlikely. But – here comes the big "but"– not impossible.<strong><br /></strong></em><br /><br /><em>I also reviewed this book over on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/">Pretty Books</a>.</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14561269441045718003">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/2658311-notgettingenough" class="left imgcol" title="notgettingenough "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1258115161p2/2658311.jpg" alt="notgettingenough " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/434619831?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2658311-notgettingenough" class="user" title="notgettingenough ">notgettingenough </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2658311-notgettingenough?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2658311-notgettingenough?shelf=haven-t-read-but" class="actionLinkLite">haven-t-read-but</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer434619831">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9571050842259751931"><br />The trouble with this movie, is that we are supposed to cheer for the wrong side. The premise, for those who haven’t read or seen it, is that the witches have a practically foolproof plan to turn all the children of the UK into mice. <br /><br />I mean, what’s not to like? <br /><br />You may say I shouldn’t have been watching this movie with a cat. It’s true, the cat and I have never been more on the same wave length. As I sat there biting my nails and screaming at those witches ‘not the soup, please don’t eat the cre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9571050842259751931"><br />The trouble with this movie, is that we are supposed to cheer for the wrong side. The premise, for those who haven’t read or seen it, is that the witches have a practically foolproof plan to turn all the children of the UK into mice. <br /><br />I mean, what’s not to like? <br /><br />You may say I shouldn’t have been watching this movie with a cat. It’s true, the cat and I have never been more on the same wave length. As I sat there biting my nails and screaming at those witches ‘not the soup, please don’t eat the cress soup’ (because a boy mouse had put the spell into it, so that the witches were to get a taste of their own medicine, so to speak), the cat was rigid with anger, hair, whiskers, tail, you name it, it was standing on end. This cat will never speak to Roald Dahl again. How dare he dangle such a prize in front of him, the most delightfully plump, tender young mice, and then take it away like that?<br /><br />Signed NGE and..<em>okay</em>...go on: <br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Cat paw" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380237807i/681481.jpg" /></a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9571050842259751931">...more</a>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1218946-kimberly-sabatini?shelf=mg-ya" class="actionLinkLite">mg-ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer588708019">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9179284443390128209">I'll be honest. My boys and I LOVE Roald Dahl books. All of them. Rather than review this book in my predictably gushy manner, I thought I would tell you a funny story that happened during our nightly reading sessions...<br /><br />For those unfamiliar with the story, a grandmother is instructing her grandson on the multiple ways one might recognize a witch in disguise. While giving this info to my eight year old, he checked me over to confirm that I was indeed, not a witch. When he heard they wore itchy wi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9179284443390128209">I'll be honest. My boys and I LOVE Roald Dahl books. All of them. Rather than review this book in my predictably gushy manner, I thought I would tell you a funny story that happened during our nightly reading sessions...<br /><br />For those unfamiliar with the story, a grandmother is instructing her grandson on the multiple ways one might recognize a witch in disguise. While giving this info to my eight year old, he checked me over to confirm that I was indeed, not a witch. When he heard they wore itchy wigs, he checked my hair line. He investigated my toes and fingers for cat like claws and block like feet without toes.I thought I'd passed inspection, but a few days later, I caught him staring deeply into my eyes. (There had been a mention of a witches pupils being multicolored.) After a good hard look, he pronounced that I was definitely not a witch--I didn't have multicolored NIPPLES. I corrected him and indicated that he meant PUPILS. His response was...whatever...it's the same thing.<br /><br />And there you have folks. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1407155741">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407155741" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3461034-trish" class="left imgcol" title="Trish"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1436099209p2/3461034.jpg" alt="Trish" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1407155741?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3461034-trish" class="user" title="Trish">Trish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17242189-the-witches" title="Paperback 9780141346410" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1407155741">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5107188943014512229">I know the story of <strong>Matilda</strong> but only from the film adaptation so <strong>The Witches</strong> was my first book by Roald Dahl. The story seemed oddly familiar and I think I might have read it when I was younger (in school perhaps?) or may have seen the movie (I googled, there is one with Anjelica Houston as The Grand High Witch) but I can't remember.<br /><br /><img width="400" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444223105i/16471898.jpg" /><br /><br />Anyway, the story was quite good. A little creepy, a little weird, a little funny, a little adventurous - the perfect mix.<br />I've heard people say that this was too sca</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5107188943014512229">I know the story of <strong>Matilda</strong> but only from the film adaptation so <strong>The Witches</strong> was my first book by Roald Dahl. The story seemed oddly familiar and I think I might have read it when I was younger (in school perhaps?) or may have seen the movie (I googled, there is one with Anjelica Houston as The Grand High Witch) but I can't remember.<br /><br /><img width="400" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444223105i/16471898.jpg" /><br /><br />Anyway, the story was quite good. A little creepy, a little weird, a little funny, a little adventurous - the perfect mix.<br />I've heard people say that this was too scary for children but I don't think so. I guess it just depends on your child. I, myself, would have definitely enjoyed this story even at the age of only 8.<br /><br />The only thing that I noticed was the age of the story itself. It was written/published in 1983 and some things written here are very ... out-of-date? ... would be considered in poor taste?<br />Example: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ When Grandmamma gives us a lesson in how to recognize a witch, the baldness is mentioned and how a bald woman was disgusting to look at. I would think that this isn't something an author would say nowadays. Just think of women that are bald due to cancer treatments or a genetic mutation. Nobody would want them to feel "disgusting" for how they look. I hope. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Moreover, although it is a common concept <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[the whole thing about dying together is not something I support. People say it all the time like "at least they died together" when someone dies in a plane crash for example but it always leaves a bitter taste in my mouth. I understand that people don't want to be left behind by their loved ones but still ... So imagine how I felt when at the end of the book Grandmamma said that a mouse-person was living for about 9 years and the little boy (!) replied that that is fantastic because then they can die togther! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Also, and I'm fully aware that this is an unpopular opinion, I think that any pet is a family member. And not one family member is more important than another. All should be equally important so <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[when Grandmamma was telling Mr. Jenkins to get rid of the cat because Bruno was more important, that didn't sit right with me. Especially when one takes into consideration how many pets get abandoned or even killed each year when they become "a liability" to their owners! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />That put me off a little.<br /><br />To make up for these three things, sort of, there was one line that was simply perfect however:<br /><em>"It doesn't matter who you are or what you look like so long as somebody loves you."</em><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444223105i/16471899.gif" /><br /><br />All in all, the story was written in a slightly amusing, dark-humoured style (with the occasional side blow on society and norms, such as certain disciplinary actions at schools at the time) with quite some thrills in the middle and it was indeed spooky. Great October/Halloween material.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5107188943014512229">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer93085107">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16625795851461593893">This is a dark-edged children's tale about a group of witches who despise children who they believe smell like "dogs droppings". These witches don't hold back their hatred for these "small piles of filth" and at their annual meeting they devise a plan to rid the earth of these vomit inducing creatures by turning them into mice and exterminating them. What they haven't planned on is the ingenuity of one brave little boy who overhears their dastardly plans and does his best to thwart them.<br /><br />This boo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16625795851461593893">This is a dark-edged children's tale about a group of witches who despise children who they believe smell like "dogs droppings". These witches don't hold back their hatred for these "small piles of filth" and at their annual meeting they devise a plan to rid the earth of these vomit inducing creatures by turning them into mice and exterminating them. What they haven't planned on is the ingenuity of one brave little boy who overhears their dastardly plans and does his best to thwart them.<br /><br />This book is a lot of fun and though it portrays witches in a pretty bad light it's not all anti-women and is all in good fun. Grandmamma is a fantastic character, described as a "tough old bird", she smokes cigars and I can't help but think it's her influence alone that has made the hero of this tale such a brave, clever little guy.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_854552622">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/854552622?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6679618-christina" class="user" title="Christina">Christina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6679618-christina?shelf=paranormal" class="actionLinkLite">paranormal</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6679618-christina?shelf=2014-snakes-n-ladders" class="actionLinkLite">2014-snakes-n-ladders</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer854552622'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer854552622">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10985449747821341269">Our main protagonist is a young boy, who lost his parents in a car accident. He is left with his loving 86 year old grandmother in Norway, who tells him the most scariest and most questionable stories about Real Witches. They relocate to England, following his parents' wishes and there, our protagonist has his first terrifying encounter with a Real Witch, with all the tell tale signs - gloves, large nose-holes, queer eyes, hair that looks like a wig and a bluish tinge on her teeth!<br /><br />The protagonis</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10985449747821341269">Our main protagonist is a young boy, who lost his parents in a car accident. He is left with his loving 86 year old grandmother in Norway, who tells him the most scariest and most questionable stories about Real Witches. They relocate to England, following his parents' wishes and there, our protagonist has his first terrifying encounter with a Real Witch, with all the tell tale signs - gloves, large nose-holes, queer eyes, hair that looks like a wig and a bluish tinge on her teeth!<br /><br />The protagonist's grandmother comes down with pneumonia and so they are unable to go to Norway in the Easter holidays, as originally planned. Instead, they take a trip to Hotel Magnificent on the south coast of England. Here our protagonist has his second encounter, this time with 85 witches including the Grand High Witch(!), all disguised as members of the RSPCC (Royal Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Children) - oh the irony! <br /><br />He overhears the Witches' schemes of opening sveet shops all over Inkland and dosing the sweets vith a potion that will turn all children into mice. Unfortunately, our protagonist is caught and falls victim to a large dosage of Formula 86 Delayed Action Mouse Maker, immediately turning him into a small furry rodent. He is able to run to his grandmother and together they come up with a brilliant plan to steal and use the Formula against the Witches. <br /><br />Hurray! Our protagonists' plan succeeds, as he drops the Formula into the Witches' soup, turning the lot of them into mice!<br /><br />The Witches is another classic Roald Dahl book that is charming and endearing. The story gave me such a laugh, yet the ending was bittersweet as our protagonist never reverts back to a boy. It was quite sad to find that he will only live up to nine years at most, alongside his grandmother (until they die old together).</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10985449747821341269">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38539442?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1432036-jesse" class="user" title="Jesse">Jesse</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=formative" class="actionLinkLite">formative</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38539442">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14816690231404888526">Was at a friend's last night, saw this on his bookshelf and couldn't resist borrowing it. Subsequently spent an enjoyable sit revisiting an old favorite. Because this <em>is</em> an old favorite--my favorite Roald Dahl book, to be exact, which means growing it was one of my VERY favorite books. Technically, it's probably a four star book--it takes a bit too long to get going and far too long to wrap up--but the nostalgia factor kicks it up to five star level. The central mock-RSPCC meeting, with its incr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14816690231404888526">Was at a friend's last night, saw this on his bookshelf and couldn't resist borrowing it. Subsequently spent an enjoyable sit revisiting an old favorite. Because this <em>is</em> an old favorite--my favorite Roald Dahl book, to be exact, which means growing it was one of my VERY favorite books. Technically, it's probably a four star book--it takes a bit too long to get going and far too long to wrap up--but the nostalgia factor kicks it up to five star level. The central mock-RSPCC meeting, with its increasingly hysterical callbacks, is such a delicious paraody of a revival meeting, managing to be both funny <em>and</em> tense. Wasn't even aware of a film version until a few years ago--probably should check that out at some point. But I can't imagine it could top the book. <br /><br /><em>"Better is not good either!" shrieked The Grand High Witch. "I demand maximum rrree-sults! So here are my orders! My orders are that every single child in this country shall be rrrubbed out, sqvashed, sqvirted, sqvittered and frrrittered before I come here again in vun year's time! Do I make myself clear?"</em><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14816690231404888526">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1126531">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1126531" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/862-bp" class="left imgcol" title="bp"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="bp" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1126531?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 09, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/862-bp" class="user" title="bp">bp</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">5th graders. And their parents. </span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1126531">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13069535435769252093">The way my life is recently, I'd be lucky to be able to finish reading the headline of the Post before having to attend to something else. <br />So in the absense of any meaningful free time in my life, I will be reviewing books from years past, the glory days when I could actually curl up on the couch and fall into a story. Or in the case of Roald Dahl, through the scary trap-door into bizarro world of teacher-witches, crazy chocolate factory owners, and insects live and chat with youngsters inside o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13069535435769252093">The way my life is recently, I'd be lucky to be able to finish reading the headline of the Post before having to attend to something else. <br />So in the absense of any meaningful free time in my life, I will be reviewing books from years past, the glory days when I could actually curl up on the couch and fall into a story. Or in the case of Roald Dahl, through the scary trap-door into bizarro world of teacher-witches, crazy chocolate factory owners, and insects live and chat with youngsters inside of giant pieces of fruit. <br /><br />I devoured authors like locusts consume crops, I'd inhale entire oeuvres if the writing merited it. And Dahl is the only one of those authors that I can remember with any clarity - mainly because his books were a little more horrifying than kids books are generally meant to be. The Witches had that sinister streak - these were real witches he was writing about, not friendly elixir mixing broombats, but nasty, bald, bloodthirsty types - animalistic in their ability to sniff out children as prey. <br /><br />There are a few images from The Witches that I will never recover from: the witches banishment of a local girl into a framed painting, where she spent her days forlornly looked out into the pasture, until she disappeared altogether from the scene. Or the realization - and acceptance - of the main character, having been turned into a mouse by the witches, and knowing that he could not return to boyhood....or the long lifespan that human beings enjoy as compared to a rodent. Even then, it was a shock to read: this child knew he would not live long, and was okay with his fate. Keep in mind.... THIS IS A CHILDREN'S BOOK! But despite the macabre lining - or maybe because of it? - I found this one of the most enduring memories of my childhood literary adventures. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13069535435769252093">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15955800691548608930">De pequeña vi la película un millón de veces, la tenía en cinta VHS original, ni siquiera grabada de la tele. Me acuerdo bastante de ella y tengo algunos fotogramas grabadísimos a fuego en la memoria y me sorprende mucho no haber leído el libro antes, pero para todo hay un momento. <br /><br />He disfrutado muchísimo la lectura, creo que tiene un humor muy particular. La abuela y el niño son encantadores, la descripción de las brujas insuperable. <br /><br />Es un libro fascinante que pueden disfrutar los adultos al 100%. Además es lo primero que leo de Roald Dahl, porque adaptaciones de sus libros he visto muchas, pero nunca había leído los originales, y me ha encantado la forma de expresarse y de narrar.<br /><br />Muy recomendable. <br /><br />Un saludo,<br />Carol Rodríguez</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1268951966">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268951966" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21766870-coos-burton" class="left imgcol" title="Coos Burton"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1434917460p2/21766870.jpg" alt="Coos Burton" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1268951966?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21766870-coos-burton" class="user" title="Coos Burton">Coos Burton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21766870-coos-burton?shelf=juveniles" class="actionLinkLite">juveniles</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21766870-coos-burton?shelf=clasicos" class="actionLinkLite">clasicos</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21766870-coos-burton?shelf=infantiles" class="actionLinkLite">infantiles</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21766870-coos-burton?shelf=brujas" class="actionLinkLite">brujas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1268951966">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1717450857206943093">Ante ustedes, una historia que de pequeña aportó un granito de arena a ese amor que fue creciendo en mi interior por el horror. Y que levante con orgullo la mano quien alguna vez tuvo un leve escalofrío al ver en la película a una de éstas brujas. Puedo decirles que a mí, personalmente, me perturbaron bastante, y a la vez me fascinaron.<br />Para los que no estén familiarizados con la historia, la historia es narrada por un chico el cual pierde a sus padres en un accidente de auto justo cuando estaban</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1717450857206943093">Ante ustedes, una historia que de pequeña aportó un granito de arena a ese amor que fue creciendo en mi interior por el horror. Y que levante con orgullo la mano quien alguna vez tuvo un leve escalofrío al ver en la película a una de éstas brujas. Puedo decirles que a mí, personalmente, me perturbaron bastante, y a la vez me fascinaron.<br />Para los que no estén familiarizados con la historia, la historia es narrada por un chico el cual pierde a sus padres en un accidente de auto justo cuando estaban viajando a la casa de su abuela. Ella se compromete a cuidarlo y a educarlo, siguiendo cautelosa la voluntad de los difuntos padres, quienes desean que vivan en su casa original en Inglaterra. Ella comienza a hablarle sobre las brujas, sobre cómo identificarlas, lo que hacen y cómo evitarlas. La curiosidad del protagonista crece, así como también su miedo. Resulta que la abuela cae enferma y se debilita, razón por la que no pueden realizar un viaje que deseaban hacer, y se quedan en un hotel grande, donde se encuentran con una convención de señoras que cumplen con las características de una bruja.<br />La historia es escabrosa, y yo creo que si lo hubiera leído de más pequeña, le hubiera temido un poco a las brujas. Especialmente, la parte en la que hace una descripción tan detallada del aspecto de una bruja, con sus uñas como garras, sus cabezas calvas, sus miradas penetrantes y sus narices puntiagudas que pueden oler a los niños con gran facilidad.<br />La historia puede resultar espeluznante, pero la lección al final es de oro, como en prácticamente todas las historias del magnífico Roald Dahl. Es definitivamente algo que recomendaría a cualquier menor para Halloween, ya que viene muy bien. <br /><br /><img height="200" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439947120ra/15908905.gif" /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1717450857206943093">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/6115396-anita" class="left imgcol" title="Anita"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Anita" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/202397840?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 20, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6115396-anita" class="user" title="Anita">Anita</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327.The_Witches" title="Paperback 9780590032490" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer202397840">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11605640000413267203">‘The Witches’, one of Road Dahl’s most popular tales, is about a young boy who gets turned into a mouse by the Grand High Witch of the entire world. Undeterred by this unfortunate turn of events, he goes on to steal the mouse-maker potion and turns all the witches of England into mice instead- saving the day. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book as much now as I did as a child. All the exciting twists made for a very gripping read. For children, I think that one of the main attractions will be that the b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11605640000413267203">‘The Witches’, one of Road Dahl’s most popular tales, is about a young boy who gets turned into a mouse by the Grand High Witch of the entire world. Undeterred by this unfortunate turn of events, he goes on to steal the mouse-maker potion and turns all the witches of England into mice instead- saving the day. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book as much now as I did as a child. All the exciting twists made for a very gripping read. For children, I think that one of the main attractions will be that the book excites their imagination. It is at times an inversion of reality. For example, being clean is considered a bad thing and the main character goes weeks without washing. Furthermore, Road Dahl gives the witches a variety of shocking, unbelievable features e.g. having no toes, blue spit and turning children into hotdogs, which will leave children astonished and very amused. <br /><br />Although the underlying moral is not explicit, teachers and parents could help reveal this to children and reinforce the importance of being alert and cautious. The witches were evil but yet still in their disguise looked like normal, friendly women. Children have a responsibility to try and keep themselves safe. It would be nice to follow up with the film.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11605640000413267203">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer903394260">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8830095214204971863"><strong>Bambini tremate, le streghe sono tornate!!</strong><br /><br />Questo libro mi ha riportato indietro nel tempo, addirittura a quando frequentavo la scuola elementare e la maestra di italiano ci faceva chiudere gli occhi e ascoltare la sua voce che impersonava i vari personaggi e leggeva il libro… e così non era difficile immaginarsi le streghe pelate, con unghie affilate e senza dita dei piedi…<br />Rileggendo questo libro ho rivissuto nuovamente quelle sensazioni.<br /><br />È incredibile come sia coinvolgente questa storia dolce/am</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8830095214204971863"><strong>Bambini tremate, le streghe sono tornate!!</strong><br /><br />Questo libro mi ha riportato indietro nel tempo, addirittura a quando frequentavo la scuola elementare e la maestra di italiano ci faceva chiudere gli occhi e ascoltare la sua voce che impersonava i vari personaggi e leggeva il libro… e così non era difficile immaginarsi le streghe pelate, con unghie affilate e senza dita dei piedi…<br />Rileggendo questo libro ho rivissuto nuovamente quelle sensazioni.<br /><br />È incredibile come sia coinvolgente questa storia dolce/amara. Un severo monito a tutti i bambini di non fidarsi mai degli sconosciuti, ma anche la consapevolezza che, nonostante le piccole dimensioni, si possono fare grandi imprese.<br /><br />Lo stile dello scrittore non solo è impeccabile, ma è capace di trasportarti all’interno del libro, di sentire le streghe parlare, di vedere le loro orribili facce e il loro sguardo crudele!!<br /><br />Insomma, un bellissimo libro che ha avuto il pregio aggiuntivo di farmi ritornare per un attimo un po’ bambina.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8830095214204971863">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1197948924420279497">Man, Roald Dahl is the perfect children's author. He takes kids seriously; there are real consequences for adventures here. His books are perfectly constructed - well, almost perfectly; I kept wondering what happened to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[William and Mary. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I can't imagine having a child and not having Dahl's complete works available for him or her.<br /><br />This book apparently comes under fire for being sexist, and I get that. <span id="freeTextContainer16733553465396547492"><em>”In fairy tales, witches always wear silly black hats and black cloaks, and they ride on broomsticks. But this is not a fairy-tale. This is about REAL WITCHES.”</em><br /><br />I decided to read this in support of Banned Book Week. So obviously I’m a bit behind schedule as this is my first time reading this and I know many of you had read this early on in your childhood. I’m 25 years old and am just now getting around to experiencing it. I positively adored Roald Dahl’s writing and am quite surprised that I neve</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16733553465396547492"><em>”In fairy tales, witches always wear silly black hats and black cloaks, and they ride on broomsticks. But this is not a fairy-tale. This is about REAL WITCHES.”</em><br /><br />I decided to read this in support of Banned Book Week. So obviously I’m a bit behind schedule as this is my first time reading this and I know many of you had read this early on in your childhood. I’m 25 years old and am just now getting around to experiencing it. I positively adored Roald Dahl’s writing and am quite surprised that I never actually read a single one of his books. <br /><br /><em>”The curtains were never drawn in that house, and through the windows I could see huge snowflakes falling slowly on to an outside world that was as black as tar.”</em><br /><br />Does it make me a total wuss to admit that this book really freaked me out a few times? And what about those pictures?! Holy crap.<br /><br /><span>[image error]</span><br />That? Is some seriously scary shit right there.<br /><br />Bottom Line… it was quite a charming little book and the relationship between the little boy and his grandmother was damn adorable. <br /><br /><u>Favorite Quote</u><br /><em>”It doesn’t matter who you are or what you look like so long as somebody loves you.”</em></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iBdmymPe2AvXJb1gTWNV77URlMvgZ7QYsD8/2VdfWuPtw1kZkQzM8Vv9ydszArNd/OZX0qm687LaNjpLm8qspg==')})
    }
  }

  }

Het boek van De Bel is nog wat grover en voor een iets oudere leeftijd geschreven. Aan het eind van het boek is nog een extra hoofdstuk opgenomen met Kriegel-spelletjes (peststreken) uit elke maand van het jaar. Het verhaal zelf eindigt niet echt overtuigend, waarbij wat in het midden blijft hoe het de zusjes verder zal vergaan. Stevig gebonden, duidelijke lay-out en niet al te lange hoofdstukken. De Kriegel-spelletjes zijn in deze editie voorzien van enkele zwartwittekeningen van De Bel zelf; verder geen illustraties. Zelf lezen vanaf ca. 10 jaar en ouder. It was published in the autumn of 1973 and has been translated into 46 languages.[1] Many of its themes are unusually dark and heavy for the children\'s book genre. Disease, death, tyranny, betrayal and rebellion are some of the dark themes that permeate the story. The lighter themes of the book involve platonic love, loyalty, hope, courage and pacifism.\n\nThe two main characters are two brothers; the older Jonatan and the younger Karl. The two brothers\' surname was originally Lion, but they are generally known as Lionheart. Karl\'s nickname is Skorpan (Rusky) since Jonatan likes these typical Swedish toasts or crusts.\n\nIn Nangijala, a land in &amp;quot;the campfires and storytelling days&amp;quot;, the brothers experience adventures. Together with a resistance group they lead the struggle against the evil Tengil, who rules with the aid of the fearsome fire-breathing dragon, Katla.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">About Roald Dahl</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl"><img alt="4273" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1311554908p2/4273.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16111166866622823852">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was Shot Down Over Libya. Today the story is published as "A Piece of Cake". The story, about his wartime a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16111166866622823852">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was Shot Down Over Libya. Today the story is published as "A Piece of Cake". The story, about his wartime adventures, was bought by the Saturday Evening Post for $900, and propelled him into a career as a writer. Its title was inspired by a highly inaccurate and sensationalized article about the crash that blinded him, which claimed he had been shot down instead of simply having to land because of low fuel.<br /><br />His first children's book was The Gremlins, about mischievous little creatures that were part of RAF folklore. The book was commissioned by Walt Disney for a film that was never made, and published in 1943. Dahl went on to create some of the best-loved children's stories of the 20th century, such as Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, Matilda and James and the Giant Peach.<br /><br />He also had a successful parallel career as the writer of macabre adult short stories, usually with a dark sense of humour and a surprise ending. Many were originally written for American magazines such as Ladies Home Journal, Harper's, Playboy and The New Yorker, then subsequently collected by Dahl into anthologies, gaining world-wide acclaim. Dahl wrote more than 60 short stories and they have appeared in numerous collections, some only being published in book form after his death. His stories also brought him three Edgar Awards: in 1954, for the collection Someone Like You; in 1959, for the story The Landlady; and in 1980, for the episode of Tales of the Unexpected based on "Skin".</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16111166866622823852">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/105046-the-witches">Quotes from The Witches</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">

            </nobr>

          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“She might even be your lovely school-teacher who is reading these words to you at this very moment. Look carefully at that teacher. Perhaps she is smiling at the absurdity of such a suggestion. Don't let that put you off. It could be part of cleverness.<br /><br />I am not, of course, telling you for one second that your teacher actually is a witch. All I am saying is that she might be one. It is most unlikely. But--here comes the big "but"--not impossible.”</span>
